class="a-row">           <div id="revMH" class="a-column a-span11">                  <h3 class="a-spacing-small">Most Helpful Customer Reviews</h3> <div id="revMHRL" class="a-section">                            <div id="rev-dpReviewsMostHelpfulAUI-R2W65ANVTVHHPO" class="a-section"><div class="a-row a-spacing-micro"><span class="a-size-small a-color-secondary">84 of 117 people found the following review helpful</span><div class="a-icon-row a-spacing-none"><a class="a-link-normal a-text-normal a-color-base" title="3.0 out of 5 stars" href="http://www.amazon.com/review/R2W65ANVTVHHPO/ref=cm_cr_dp_title/178-8721136-5538508?ie=UTF8&ASIN=B0077R5KXG&channel=detail-glance&nodeID=172282&store=electronics"><i class="a-icon a-icon-star a-star-3"></i></a><span class="a-letter-space"></span><a class="a-link-normal a-text-normal a-color-base" href="http://www.amazon.com/review/R2W65ANVTVHHPO/ref=cm_cr_dp_title/178-8721136-5538508?ie=UTF8&ASIN=B0077R5KXG&channel=detail-glance&nodeID=172282&store=electronics"><span class="a-size-base a-text-bold">CES Experience - Great Product, but wait it out</span></a></div><span class="a-color-secondary">              <span class="a-size-normal">     <span class="a-color-secondary">       By     </span>     <a href="/gp/pdp/profile/A25CP0NQR6XJ8F/ref=cm_cr_dp_pdp/178-8721136-5538508" class="noTextDecoration">TJ Weber</a>   </span> <span class="a-color-secondary"> on January 13, 2013</span></span></div><div id="revData-dpReviewsMostHelpfulAUI-R2W65ANVTVHHPO" class="a-row a-spacing-small">      <div class="a-section">   I experienced this during a private demonstration at CES (Consumer Electronics Show) this year.  Sony gave a very nice pitch that since most movies are filmed in 4k or higher, getting content to a 4k media server is going to be coming "very soon".  Sony demonstrated two forms of content.  The first format was a James Bond trailer for their upcoming movie, directly from a 4k server.  It was flawless, and in fact if you pay too close attention to the details, you really can see too much with the picture.  Regardless, the action on the movie trailer was almost straight out from the theater.<br><br>The second format presented was a clip from a Tony Bennett concert on Blu Ray up-scaled to 4k.  I did not see much of a difference between the up-scaled version and watching it on a regular 1080p projector.  I currently have a Sony VPLHW30ES projecting on a 170" diagonal screen.<br><br>My major disappointment?  CONTENT.  It's very nice that we're embarking on the Ultra HD / 4K avenue of television, but it would be hard for the average consumer to justify spending this price unless you are creating your own content.  Apple did not release the iPod without content to go along with it -- so unless you are shooting, editing, or doing private screenings of your own 4k content, I say wait it out until the prices drop below $5k. </div>  </div>             <a class="a-link-normal comment-link" title="12" There is ONE 4 k move out there, the new 007 skyfall. I guess you can rent it though Sony but the wait list is like a year or more. It comes on a hard drive that is like a few terrabytes.<br>Long story short is it is awesome but similar to owning a blu ray player and only using DVD discs on it.<br>My buddy has lots of money, but We work with a lot of fixtures for projecting media during events.<br><br>4k projectors are necesarry for live outdoor events that are in need of video projection.  The art is called projection mapping and its becoming more and more popular.<br><br>The 4k projection bulbs are extremely bright and strong. How bright?  Well in England, a 360 foot high building was used as the screen while 16 projectors were set up over 900 feet away. The images are stunning. The video is available at online just search "Deadmau5 London"<br><br>A handfull of companies are turning to Projection Mapping for advertising. Displaying eye catching imagery on theyre store fronts via a 4k projector set up somewhere in the distance luminating the entire building.  A local San Diegan is one example of someone to call if you need your venue to have a little extra spice. You can also see lots of videos of his work by searching "seeper"<br><br>This technology is slowly becoming more and more affordable and is being utilized more frequently for practical purposes such as the aforementioned. Anyone who is considering swapping out theyre home projector for on of these to get a little better picture at the house to watch sports center, the technology isnt there yet because tv is not broadcasted in resolutions that high. Sorry, your stuck with 1080i and will be so for many many years to come. The same holds true for video games and movie projection.<br><br>Unless you are in NEED of this device for a job or event and you have adequate media to run on it already in hand, youd be better off renting out a theater for the day and would probably save money.<br><br>The sad truth is that anyone who is reading this right now. Has no need for this product </div>  </div>             <a class="a-link-normal comment-link" title="5"
